The Definition and Linguistic Origin of Taqwa
Al-Sawi defines taqwa technically and linguistically, citing al-Razi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that taqwa linguistically means protection and technically means obeying Allah by performing commands and avoiding prohibitions.

Core Idea
Taqwa is not just fear; it is a shield of obedience against sin.

In this passage, al-Sawi unpacks the meaning of taqwa, drawing from Imam al-Razi's linguistic analysis and the technical definition used by scholars. Understanding this dual meaning helps us appreciate the comprehensive nature of piety. The passage is a detailed exegetical note from a classical commentary.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the words 'التقوى' and 'التقى'. Then read the translation.
2
Identify the two aspects of taqwa
Notice that the passage gives both a technical definition (performing commands, avoiding prohibitions) and a linguistic origin (protection).
3
Understand the metaphor of the shield
Al-Razi explains that taqwa is like a shield that protects from sin. Reflect on how this metaphor shapes the concept.
4
Review the scholarly citation
The definition is transmitted from al-Razi via al-Laqani, showing the chain of knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تِلتَ) أي : أدركت (التَّقى) أي: التقوى، وهي امتثال المأمورات الاتقاء، فعلاً والمَنهيَّاتِ تركاً . قال الإمام الرازي : التَّقى والتَّقوى واحد، وهما لغة: بمعنى اتخاذ وهو الوقاية؛ أي: ما يقي الشَّخص ؛ يعني : يحفظه ويحول بينه وبين ما يخافه؛ مثل الترس ونحوه في الأجسام، فكأنَّ المعنى: جعل بينه وبين المعاصي وقاية تحول بينه وبينها، من قوَّة عَزْمِه على تَرْكِها واستحضار علمه ،بقُبحها، نقله الشيخ عبد السلام اللقاني في شرح الجزائرية» (۱). وهذه الجملة إنشائية في المعنى، قصد بها الدُّعاءَ قوله : (فكأن المعنى ... إلخ) : التفت الشيخ إلى أنَّ المراد بالتَّقوى: الخوف من الله تعالى، الناشئ عنه عدم صدور ما يغضب الله تعالى. قوله : ( إنشائية في المعنى) : أي : خبريَّة في اللفظ. (۱) فتح المجيد بكفاية المريد (ق/ ۱۳۱)،
(You attained [تِلتَ]) i.e., you perceived, (piety [التَّقى]) i.e., al-taqwā, which is performing commands [امتثال المأمورات] and avoiding prohibitions [المَنهيَّاتِ تركاً] by action and abandonment. Imam al-Rāzī said: 'al-tuqā and al-taqwā are one, and they are linguistically in the sense of اتخاذ [taking] which is protection; i.e., that which protects the person, meaning it preserves him and interposes between him and what he fears; like a shield and its like among bodies. So it is as if the meaning is: he places between himself and sins a protection that interposes between him and them, from the strength of his resolve to abandon them and his presence of mind of their ugliness.' Transmitted by Shaykh ʿAbd al-Salām al-Laqānī in his commentary on al-Jazāʾiriyya (1). And this sentence [i.e., the poet's line] is declarative in meaning, intended as supplication. His statement: 'As if the meaning... etc.': The Shaykh [i.e., al-Sanūsī?] turned to the point that the intended meaning of taqwā is fear of God, exalted, from which arises not performing that which angers God. His statement: 'Declarative in meaning': i.e., it is informative in wording. (1) Fatḥ al-Majīd bi-Kifāyat al-Murīd (folio 131).
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exegetical note on the meaning of the word 'التقوى' (taqwā, piety) as it appears in the poem being commented upon. It begins by explaining the line of the poem: 'تِلتَ التَّقى' meaning 'you attained piety'. Then it defines taqwā technically as performing commanded acts and avoiding prohibited ones. Imam al-Rāzī is then quoted to give the linguistic derivation: taqwā comes from the root 'و-ق-ي' meaning protection, like a shield. So the pious person creates a barrier between himself and sins through resolve and knowledge. This definition is transmitted by al-Laqānī. Then the hashiah comments on the sentence structure: the poet's line is declarative in wording but imperative in meaning (إنشائية في المعنى), intended as a supplication (دعاء) that God make the person achieve taqwā. The commentary notes that the intended meaning of taqwā in this context is fear of God that prevents disobedience.

Key Terms
تقوى
تقى
اتخاذ
وقاية
امتثال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Taqwā only means fear of God.
Correction: Taqwā includes active obedience and avoidance of sin, as well as the foundational fear that motivates such actions.

Checkpoint

B) Protection

D) Praise

Key Takeaway

The Supplicatory Meaning of Declarative Sentences
Al-Sawi notes that the poet's line is declarative in form but a supplication in meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a declarative sentence in Arabic can function as a supplication, as seen in the line about taqwa.

Core Idea
In Arabic, a declarative sentence can carry the force of a prayer.

This passage also includes a grammatical observation: the poet's line 'You attained piety' is declarative in wording but intended as a supplication. This subtlety is common in Arabic, and understanding it enriches our interpretation of religious texts. The hashiah provides this insight to clarify the poet's intention.

Guided Path
1
Read the relevant part
Focus on the phrase 'وهذه الجملة إنشائية في المعنى' and its explanation. Read the translation.
2
Understand the term 'إنشائية'
Note that إنشائية means 'performative' or 'imperative' in meaning, even though the form is خبر (declarative).
3
Reflect on the context
The line is from a poem praising the Prophet? Actually it's a supplication for the reader to attain piety. Think about how this affects the interpretation.
4
Review the commentary
The hashiah explains that the intended meaning is a prayer that God grant the person taqwa.

The Dual Purpose of the Poet's Line: Supplication and Completion
Al-Sawi comments on the dual purpose of a line from the poem.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dual purpose of the poet's line: it is both a supplication for piety and a grammatical completion of the verse.

Core Idea
The poet's line is both a prayer and a structural completion.

This passage from al-Sawi's hashiah explains a key line in the opening poem. The line that says 'for the one who seeks to know God's attributes' is actually more than a statement of purpose—it is a supplication to Allah. Al-Sawi breaks down the grammar to show the poet intended two things at once.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Notice the flow of the commentary.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the two intended purposes
The hashiah explicitly says the poet intended two things: supplication (الدعاء) and completion (التكملة). Find these in the text.
Supplication is for the seeker to achieve piety.
3
Understand the grammatical analysis
The word 'تكملة' is in the accusative case, coordinated with 'الدعاء' as the object of 'قصد'. This shows both are part of the poet's intent.
Grammatical coordination (عطف) links the two purposes.
4
Relate to the overall work
The line's dual function reminds us that the pursuit of knowledge of God's attributes is tied to prayer for piety, blending theology and devotion.

لمن حاول معرفة صفات الله تعالى، وتكملة البيت، كأنَّه قال : اللهم ؛ اجعله محصّلاً للتّقوى. قوله : (لمن حاول معرفة صفات الله تعالى أي زاولها واشتغل بها . : قوله : ( وتكملة البيت بالنَّصب عطفاً على الدُّعاء؛ أي: فقصد بها أمرين : الدُّعاء والتكملة .
For the one who seeks to know God's attributes, and the completion of the verse, as if he said: 'O Allah, make him an achiever of piety.' His statement: 'For the one who seeks to know God's attributes' i.e., he undertakes it and occupies himself with it. His statement: 'And the completion of the verse' in the accusative, coordinated as a conjunction with 'the supplication'; i.e., so he intended by it two things: the supplication and the completion.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a brief commentary on a line of the poem that states the purpose of the work: it is for the one who seeks to know God's attributes. The hashiah explains that the line includes both a supplication (دعاء) to God to make the seeker achieve piety (تقوى) and a grammatical completion of the verse structure. The expression 'تكملة البيت' (completion of the verse) is parsed as an accusative object coordinated with 'الدُّعاء', indicating that the poet aimed at two things: offering a supplication and completing the poetic meter of the line.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'تكملة البيت' is a separate phrase unrelated to the supplication.
Correction: It is syntactically linked to the supplication as a coordinated object, showing both are part of the poet's single intent.

Checkpoint
What two things did the poet intend according to the hashiah?
A) Supplication and praise
B) Supplication and completion of the verse
C) Knowledge and action
D) Fear and hope

Key Takeaway
The poet's line serves both as a prayer for piety and as a structural completion of the verse.
